TITLE: BRONCHOSCOPIC LUNG VOLUME REDUCTION — ENDOBRONCHIAL VALVES

Indication:
72-year-old female with severe COPD/emphysema, significant hyperinflation and dyspnea despite maximal therapy.

Pre-op Dx: Emphysema (J43.9), dyspnea (R06.00)
Post-op Dx: Same

Procedure(s):

* Bronchoscopy with endobronchial valve placement to LUL (CPT 31647; modifier -22??)
* Airway toilet

Sedation/Anesthesia:
Moderate sedation listed on nursing sheet; procedure performed under GA with LMA noted once in anesthesia record. Patient tolerated without hemodynamic instability.

Procedure in detail:
Flexible bronchoscope introduced. Tracheobronchial tree examined. No tumor. Secretions suctioned. Chartis balloon occlusion testing of LUL demonstrated pattern consistent with no collateral ventilation. Segmental measurements performed; valves deployed to apicoposterior and anterior segments and lingula (total 4 valves). Valves seated well. No bleeding.

EBL: <10 mL
Complications: None
Disposition/Plan: Observe overnight; CXR in PACU; continue bronchodilators; avoid strenuous activity x 48 hrs; follow-up in IP clinic.

PROCEDURES PERFORMED:

* Flexible bronchoscopy with airway clearance
* Chartis collateral ventilation assessment (RLL)
* Endobronchial valve placement (RLL)

ANESTHESIA: General anesthesia with ETT
MONITORING: Standard ASA monitors
INSTRUMENTS: Therapeutic bronchoscope; Chartis catheter; sizing kit; valves (multiple sizes)

PROCEDURE IN DETAIL:
Time-out performed. Bronchoscope advanced via ETT. Airway survey demonstrated moderate tracheobronchomalacia and scattered mucous plugging, suctioned. No endobronchial lesion. Balloon occlusion testing of RLL performed with stable tracings suggesting absence of collateral ventilation. Segmental sizing performed sequentially. Valves deployed to RLL superior segment and basal segments (total 5). One valve was repositioned for improved seating. Final inspection showed no active bleeding, no valve dislodgement, and improved occlusion of targeted segments.

SPECIMENS: None
EBL: Minimal
COMPLICATIONS: None
DISPOSITION: PACU then inpatient observation.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EDGE_CASE_TAGS: missing_section, malformed_codes
PRE/POST DX: Tracheal stenosis (J39.8)

PROCEDURE:

* Bronchoscopy with laser ablation of tracheal granulation tissue (CPT “31641?? laser”)
* Balloon dilation

ANESTHESIA: GA

DETAIL:
[PATIENT] 36-year-old female with post-intubation tracheal stenosis and granulation. Bronchoscopy showed focal stenosis with granulation tissue. Laser applied in controlled fashion to granulation, followed by balloon dilation to improve airway diameter. Final inspection showed improved patency and minimal oozing.

EBL: <10 mL
COMPLICATIONS: none
PLAN: PPI, inhaled steroid course, repeat evaluation in 4–8 weeks.

ROBOTIC BRONCHOSCOPY OPERATIVE NOTE

Patient: [PATIENT] (58-year-old male)
Indication: Peripheral RUL nodule (R91.1) requiring tissue diagnosis

Pre-op Dx: Lung nodule (R91.1)
Post-op Dx: Same

Procedure(s):

* Robotic-assisted navigational bronchoscopy to RUL lesion
* Radial ultrasound confirmation
* Transbronchial biopsy + brush + BAL
* Linear EBUS-TBNA of station 7 (staging) (31652??)

Anesthesia: GA with ETT
EBL: <10 mL
Complications: none

Technique:
Robotic platform docked. Registration performed. Path planned to RUL posterior segment lesion. Advanced to target, then radial ultrasound showed eccentric view; adjusted one airway more distal with improved concentric signal. Fluoroscopy used for confirmation. Biopsies obtained:
• TBBx x6 (RUL lesion)
• Brush x2
• BAL 60 mL instilled, 22 mL returned
Then linear EBUS performed; station 7 sampled, 3 passes.

Specimens:
A: RUL lesion TBBx
B: RUL brush
C: BAL RUL
D: Station 7 TBNA

Plan:
CXR in PACU; routine post-bronchoscopy care; follow cytology/pathology.

ENDOBRONCHIAL VALVES FOR PNEUMOTHORAX — PROCEDURE NOTE

Patient: [PATIENT] (45-year-old male)
Indication: Persistent air leak after secondary spontaneous pneumothorax with chest tube in place.

Pre Dx: Pneumothorax (J93.9), persistent air leak (J95.811?)
Post Dx: Same

Procedure(s):

* Flexible bronchoscopy
* Balloon occlusion localization
* Endobronchial valve placement for air leak control (CPT: 31647? / “valve for PAL”)

Anesthesia: Moderate sedation (sometimes)
Sedation meds: fentanyl 50 mcg + midazolam 2 mg IV (times variably documented)

Technique:
Airway inspected; no lesion. Sequential balloon occlusion performed to localize air leak based on chest tube bubbling reduction. Greatest reduction with occlusion of RUL. Two valves deployed to suspected segmental bronchi. After deployment, bubbling markedly decreased from continuous to intermittent. Hemostasis confirmed.

Complications: none
EBL: minimal
Plan: Continue chest tube to water seal trial; CXR; reassess air leak over 24–48 hrs.

EDGE_CASE_TAGS: extreme_length, table_with_tabs
COMBINED COMPLEX CASE (Template E)

Patient: [PATIENT], 70-year-old male
Indication: Two peripheral nodules (RUL + RLL) and mediastinal staging prior to definitive therapy.

Pre-op Dx:

* Multiple pulmonary nodules (R91.8)
* Mediastinal adenopathy (R59.0)

Post-op Dx: Same

Procedures:

* Robotic bronchoscopy to RUL target + sampling
* Robotic bronchoscopy to RLL target + sampling
* Linear EBUS-TBNA stations 4R, 7, 11R
* BAL (RLL)

Anesthesia: General anesthesia with ETT
Monitoring: Standard ASA
EBL: ~15 mL
Complications: none

Workflow:

1. Registration and navigation to RUL target. Radial ultrasound initially eccentric; repositioned one generation distally with improved signal. Fluoroscopy used. TBNA x3, forceps biopsies x5, brush x1.
2. Navigation to RLL target. Concentric radial signal achieved. Cryobiopsy performed x3 with balloon occlusion in segment for hemostasis; no significant bleeding.
3. Linear EBUS performed. Stations sampled in order: 11R (2 passes), 4R (3 passes), 7 (3 passes). Doppler negative at needle paths.

TAB SUMMARY (tabs):
Site	Modality	Samples	Comment
RUL	Forceps+TBNA	9	adequate
RLL	Cryo+BAL	4+1	balloon used
4R	EBUS-TBNA	3	—
7	EBUS-TBNA	3	—
11R	EBUS-TBNA	2	—

Specimens:
A: RUL TBNA
B: RUL TBBx
C: RUL brush
D: RLL cryobiopsy
E: RLL BAL
F: 11R TBNA
G: 4R TBNA
H: 7 TBNA

Plan:
CXR in PACU; routine post-bronchoscopy monitoring; follow cytology/pathology; consider CT chest in 2–4 weeks if non-diagnostic.
